 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><B>Exhibit 99.1 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>EAGLE FINANCIAL SERVICES, INC. ANNOUNCES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>2015 SECOND QUARTER FINANCIAL RESULTS </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">


<TR>
<TD WIDTH="11%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="1%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="44%"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom" WIDTH="1%"></TD>
<TD WIDTH="43%"></TD></TR>


<TR STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">
<TD VALIGN="top"><B>Contact:</B></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"><B>Kathleen J. Chappell, Vice President and CFO</B></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"><B>540-955-2510</B></TD></TR>
<TR STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">
<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="bottom"></TD>
<TD VALIGN="top"><B><U>kchappell@bankofclarke.com</U></B></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>BERRYVILLE, VIRGINIA </B>(July 23, 2015) &#150; Eagle Financial Services, Inc. (OTCQX: <B>EFSI</B>), the holding company
for Bank of Clarke County, whose divisions include Eagle Investment Group, today announced second quarter net income and overall strong financial performance. Select highlights for the second quarter 2015 include: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Loan growth of $24.6 million </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Deposit growth of $13.1 million </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Net income of $798,000 </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Net Interest Margin of 4.13% </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I></I>John R. Milleson, President and CEO, stated <I>&#147;We are extremely
pleased with the strong balance sheet growth experienced in the second quarter and are encouraged by the potential our newer retail branches provide. Although the quarter&#146;s income was negatively impacted by the purchase of the property on which
one of our Winchester, VA retail branches is located, we expect the future benefit of ownership of this property will offset this current expense. We continue to expand our footprint in Loudoun County, VA and anticipate opening our fourth retail
branch in Leesburg, VA during the third quarter of 2015. We believe that the new growth in Loudoun County and the extensive presence that we have in our existing markets will allow the Company to continue to provide its shareholders a positive
return and consistent dividends.&#148; </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Income Statement Review </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net income for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 decreased 45.15% to $798,000 when compared to the $1.5 million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015.
Net income for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 was $1.2 million below net income for the same period in 2014. Much of the decrease related to the June 2015 purchase of land on which one of the Company&#146;s retail branches is located. While
the Company owns the branch building, the land had previously been leased. On June&nbsp;10, 2015, the Company purchased the land, subject to the existing lease, and recorded it at market value, resulting in a $520,000 write down of the total
purchase price. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net interest income increased $254,000 or 4.58% from $5.5 million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015 to $5.8 million for the
quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015. This increase in net interest income was driven primarily by the increased loan volume experienced by the Bank. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net
interest income decreased 1.93% or $114,000 from $5.9 million for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2014 to $5.8 million for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015. This decrease is attributed to declining asset yields. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total loan interest income was $5.4 and $5.3 million for the quarters ended June&nbsp;30 and March&nbsp;31, 2015, respectively. For the quarter ended
June&nbsp;30, 2014, total loan interest income was $5.6 million. Average loans for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 were $470.6 million compared to $466.1 million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. Total average accruing loans were
$463.8 million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and $458.5 million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. For the second quarter of 2014, total average loans were $463.8 million and average accruing loans were $457.3 million. The
tax equivalent yield on average loans for the quarters ended June&nbsp;30 and March&nbsp;31, 2015 was 4.65% and 4.64%, respectively. The tax equivalent yield on loans for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2014 was 4.85%. Interest income from the
investment portfolio was $678,000 for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and $626,000 for the same period ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. Average investments were $103.0 million for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and $96.3 million for the quarter
ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. Interest income from the investment portfolio was $806,000 for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2014 while average investments were $103.9 million for the same time period. Although the Company has higher levels of average
investments due to the excess cash balances being deployed into the investment portfolio during the first few months of 2015, income from the investment portfolio has declined due to declining investment yields. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total interest expense was $327,000 for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and $398,000 for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. The average cost of
interest bearing liabilities decreased seven basis points when comparing the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 to the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. The average balance of interest bearing liabilities decreased $5.1 million from the quarter ended
March&nbsp;31, 2015. The net interest margin was 4.13% for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 and 4.02% for the quarter March&nbsp;31, 2015. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2014, total interest expense was $488,000 and the net interest margin was
4.32%. Managing excess cash and continued monitoring of other funding costs has helped stabilize the Company&#146;s net interest margin in the face of declining asset yields. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company&#146;s net interest margin is not a measurement under accounting principles generally accepted in the United States, but it is a common measure
used by the financial services industry to determine how profitably earning assets are funded. The Company&#146;s net interest margin is calculated by dividing tax equivalent net interest income by total average earning assets. Tax equivalent net
interest income is calculated by grossing up interest income for the amounts that are non-taxable (i.e., municipal income) then subtracting interest expense. The tax rate utilized is 34%. The table at the end of this document reconciles
tax-equivalent net interest income, which is not a measurement under accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America (GAAP), to net interest income. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Non-interest income was $1.6 million for the quarters ended June&nbsp;30 and March&nbsp;31, 2015. Other service charges and fees increased $174,000 or 23.02%
when comparing the three months ended June&nbsp;30 to March&nbsp;31, 2015. The majority of this increase resulted from the increase in fees from ATMs and non-deposit investment sales. When comparing the quarter ended June&nbsp;30 2015 to the same
period in 2014, other service charges and fees increased $103,000 or 12.45%. When comparing the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 to the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015, fees from fiduciary activities decreased $72,000 or 16.82%. This decrease
results mostly from some one time fees collected during the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. Fees from fiduciary activities decreased $6,000 or 1.66% from the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 to the same period in 2014. Noninterest income for the
three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2014 was $1.6 million. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Noninterest expense was $6.1 million for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015. This represents an
increase of $1.1 million or 21.24% and $1.2 million or 23.46% from the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2015 and June&nbsp;30, 2014, respectively. Much of these increases resulted from the adjustment to the purchase price of land acquired in June 2015.
On June&nbsp;10, 2015, the Company purchased the land, subject to the existing lease, and recorded it at market value, resulting in a $520,000 write down of the total purchase price. Other components of non-interest expense, including salaries and
employees&#146; benefits, occupancy expenses and advertising and marketing expenses have also increased with the Company&#146;s hiring of additional employees for and the opening of new facilities in Loudoun County, Virginia. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Asset Quality and Provision for Loan Losses </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Nonperforming assets consist of loans 90 days past due and still accruing interest, nonaccrual loans, other real estate owned (foreclosed properties), and
repossessed assets. At June&nbsp;30, 2015, nonperforming asset remained relatively unchanged at $9.1 million. During the second quarter of 2015, the Bank placed two loans on non-accrual status. Management regularly evaluates the financial condition
of borrowers with loans on non-accrual status and the value of any collateral on these loans. The results of these evaluations are used to estimate the amount of losses which may be realized on the disposition of these non-accrual loans. The
majority of the non-accrual loans are secured by real estate. One real estate asset had been foreclosed upon during the second quarter of 2015 and the Bank sold three pieces of other real estate owned recorded at a net value of $366,000 during the
same period. Loans greater than 90 days past due and still accruing increased from $63,000 at March&nbsp;31, 2015 to $68,000 at June&nbsp;30, 2015. Nonperforming assets were $8.3 million or 1.38% of total assets at June&nbsp;30, 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company may, under certain circumstances, restructure loans in troubled debt restructurings as a concession to a borrower when the borrower is
experiencing financial distress. Formal, standardized loan restructuring programs are not utilized by the Company. Each loan considered for restructuring is evaluated based on customer circumstances and may include modifications to one or more loan
provision. Such restructured loans are included in impaired loans but may not necessarily be nonperforming loans. At June&nbsp;30, 2015, the Company had 25 troubled debt restructurings totaling $7.6 million, of which 21 loans, totaling $6.7 million,
were considered performing loans. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company realized $64,000 in net recoveries for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015 compared to $41,000 in net
charge offs for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2015. Net recoveries for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2014 were $437,000. The Company continues to operate a troubled credit group to monitor past due loans, identify potential problem
credits, and develop action plans to work through its troubled loans as promptly as possible. Asset quality remains a primary focus of the Company. Necessary resources continue to be devoted to the ongoing review of the loan portfolio and the
workouts of problem assets to minimize any losses to the Company. Management will continue to monitor delinquencies, risk rating changes, charge-offs, market trends and other indicators of risk in the Company&#146;s portfolio, particularly those
tied to residential and commercial real estate, and adjust the allowance for loan losses accordingly. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company recorded a provision for loan losses of $300,000 for the quarter ended June&nbsp;30, 2015. Provisions
for loan losses were $133,000 and negative $283,000 for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2015 and June&nbsp;30, 2014, respectively. The allowance for loan losses was $5.5 million, or 1.14% of total outstanding loans, at June&nbsp;30, 2015. At
March&nbsp;31, 2015 and June&nbsp;30, 2014, the allowance for loan losses was $5.2 million and $5.9 million, respectively. The amount of provision for loan losses during each quarter reflects the results of the Bank&#146;s analysis used to determine
the adequacy of the allowance for loan losses. The Company is committed to maintaining an allowance at a level that adequately reflects the risk inherent in the loan portfolio. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Total Consolidated Assets </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total consolidated assets of
the Company at June&nbsp;30, 2015 were $634.3 million, which represented an increase of $20.6 million or 3.35% from total assets of $613.7 million at March&nbsp;31, 2015. This increase was driven by the increased volume of the loan portfolio. Total
loans increased from $461.4 million at March&nbsp;31, 2015 to $486.0 at June&nbsp;30, 2015. At June&nbsp;30, 2014, total consolidated assets were $601.7 million and total loans were $464.3 million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Deposits and Other Borrowings </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Total deposits, which
include brokered deposits, were $522.8 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015. This reflects an increase of 2.57% or $13.1 million from $509.7 at March&nbsp;31, 2015. At June&nbsp;30, 2014, total deposits were $492.0 million. The Company held $11.0 million
in brokered deposits at June&nbsp;30, 2015 and March&nbsp;31, 2015. The Company held $9.9 million in brokered deposits at June&nbsp;30, 2014. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fed funds
purchased and securities sold under agreement to repurchase were $8.3 million at June&nbsp;30, 2015. At March&nbsp;31, 2015 and June&nbsp;30, 2014, fed funds purchased and securities sold under agreement to repurchase were $0. Borrowings with the
Federal Home Loan Bank of Atlanta have remained unchanged at $20.0 million when comparing June&nbsp;30 and March&nbsp;31, 2015. Borrowings with the Federal Home Loan Bank of Atlanta were $30.0 million at June&nbsp;30, 2014. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Equity </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Shareholders&#146; equity at June&nbsp;30, 2015
was $73.9 million, reflecting a decrease of $604,000 from $74.5 million at March&nbsp;31, 2015. At June&nbsp;30, 2014 shareholders&#146; equity was $70.2 million. The book value of the Company at June&nbsp;30, 2015 was $21.30 per common share. Total
common shares outstanding were 3,495,800 at June&nbsp;30, 2015. On July&nbsp;15, 2015, the board of directors declared a $0.20 per common share cash dividend for shareholders of record as of July&nbsp;30, 2015 and payable on August&nbsp;12, 2015.
</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="line-height:2.0pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:2pt;border-bottom:2.00pt solid #000000">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(1)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The net interest margin is calculated by dividing tax equivalent net interest income by total average earning assets. Tax equivalent interest income is calculated by grossing up interest income for the amounts that are
non-taxable (i.e., municipal income) then subtracting interest expense. The rate utilized is 34%. See the table below for the quarterly tax equivalent net interest income and the reconciliation of net interest income to tax equivalent net interest
income. The Company&#146;s net interest margin is a common measure used by the financial service industry to determine how profitable earning assets are funded. Because the Company earns a fair amount of non-taxable interest income due to the mix of
securities in its investment security portfolio, net interest income for the ratio is calculated on a tax equivalent basis as described above. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(2)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The efficiency ratio is not a measurement under accounting principles generally accepted in the United States. It is calculated by dividing non-interest expense by the sum of tax equivalent net interest income and
non-interest income excluding gains and losses on the investment portfolio and sales of repossessed assets. The tax rate utilized is 34%. See the table below for the quarterly tax equivalent net interest income and a reconciliation of net interest
income to tax equivalent net interest income. The Company calculates this ratio in order to evaluate its overhead structure or how effectively it is operating. An increase in the ratio from period to period indicates the Company is losing a larger
percentage of its income to expenses. The Company believes that the efficiency ratio is a reasonable measure of profitability. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(1)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The diluted earnings multiple is calculated by dividing the period&#146;s closing market price per share by the annualized diluted earnings per share for the period. The diluted earnings multiple is a measure of how
much an investor may be willing to pay for $1.00 of the Company&#146;s earnings. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(2)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The book value multiple (or price to book ratio) is calculated by dividing the period&#146;s closing market price per share by the period&#146;s book value per share. The book value multiple is a measure used to compare
the Company&#146;s market value per share to its book value per share. </TD></TR></TABLE>
